If not provided or None, a\n        freshly-allocated array is returned.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    out : ndarray of floats\n        An array with the same dimensions and data-type as the input.\n        If second argument is not supplied then a new array is returned\n        with the rounded values.\n\n        If a second argument is supplied the result is stored there.\n        The return value ``out`` is then a reference to that array.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    rint, trunc, floor, ceil\n    around : Round to given number of decimals\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> np.fix(3.14)\n    3.0\n    >>> np.fix(3)\n    3\n    >>> np.fix([2.1, 2.9, -2.1, -2.9])\n    array([ 2.,  2., -2., -2.])\n\n    \"\"\"\n    # promote back to an array if flattened\n    res = nx.asanyarray(nx.ceil(x, out=out))\n    res = nx.floor(x, out=res, where=nx.greater_equal(x, 0))\n\n    # when no out argument is passed and no subclasses are involved, flatten\n    # scalars\n    if out is None and type(res) is nx.ndarray:\n        res = res[()]\n    return res\n\n\n@dispatch_array_function(_dispatcher, verify=False, module='numpy')\ndef isposinf(x, out=None):\n    \"\"\"\n    Test element-wise for positive infinity, return result as bool array.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    x : array_like\n        The input array.\n    out : array_like, optional\n        A location into which the result is stored. If provided, it must have a\n        shape that the input broadcasts to. If not provided or None, a\n        freshly-allocated boolean array is returned.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    out : ndarray\n        A boolean array with the same dimensions as the input.\n        If second argument is not supplied then a boolean array is returned\n        with values True where the corresponding element of the input is\n        positive infinity and values False where the element of the input is\n        not positive infinity.\n\n        If a second argument is supplied the result is stored there. If the\n        type of that array is a numeric type the result is represented as zeros\n        and ones, if the type is boolean then as False and True.\n        The return value `out` is then a reference to that array.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    isinf, isneginf, isfinite, isnan\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    NumPy uses the IEEE Standard for Binary Floating-Point for Arithmetic\n    (IEEE 754).\n\n    Errors result if the second argument is also supplied when x is a scalar\n    input, if first and second arguments have different shapes, or if the\n    first argument has complex values\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> np.isposinf(np.inf)\n    True\n    >>> np.isposinf(-np.inf)\n    False\n    >>> np.isposinf([-np.inf, 0., np.inf])\n    array([False, False,  True])\n\n    >>> x = np.array([-np.inf, 0., np.inf])\n    >>> y = np.array([2, 2, 2])\n    >>> np.isposinf(x, y)\n    array([0, 0, 1])\n    >>> y\n    array([0, 0, 1])\n\n    \"\"\"\n    is_inf = nx.isinf(x)\n    try:\n        signbit = ~nx.signbit(x)\n    except TypeError as e:\n        dtype = nx.asanyarray(x).dtype\n        raise TypeError(f'This operation is not supported for {dtype} values '\n                        'because it would be ambiguous.') from e\n    else:\n        return nx.logical_and(is_inf, signbit, out)\n\n\n@dispatch_array_function(_dispatcher, verify=False, module='numpy')\ndef isneginf(x, out=None):\n    \"\"\"\n    Test element-wise for negative infinity, return result as bool array.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    x : array_like\n        The input array.\n    out : array_like, optional\n        A location into which the result is stored. If the\n        type of that array is a numeric type the result is represented as\n        zeros and ones, if the type is boolean then as False and True. The\n        return value `out` is then a reference to that array.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    isinf, isposinf, isnan, isfinite\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    NumPy uses the IEEE Standard for Binary Floating-Point for Arithmetic\n    (IEEE 754).\n\n    Errors result if the second argument is also supplied when x is a scalar\n    input, if first and second arguments have different shapes, or if the\n    first argument has complex values.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> np.isneginf(-np.inf)\n    True\n    >>> np.isneginf(np.inf)\n    False\n    >>> np.isneginf([-np.inf, 0., np.inf])\n    array([ True, False, False])\n\n    >>> x = np.array([-np.inf, 0., np.inf])\n    >>> y = np.array([2, 2, 2])\n    >>> np.isneginf(x, y)\n    array([1, 0, 0])\n    >>> y\n    array([1, 0, 0])\n\n    \"\"\"\n    is_inf = nx.isinf(x)\n    try:\n        signbit = nx.signbit(x)\n    except TypeError as e:\n        dtype = nx.asanyarray(x).dtype\n        raise TypeError(f'This operation is not supported for {dtype} values '\n                        'because it would be ambiguous.') from e\n    else:\n        return nx.logical_and(is_inf, signbit, out)\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":259,"cache_read_input_tokens":68796,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":259},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"b164dcc3-5d88-4121-aaa2-648fe021ecd6","uuid":"dd7030dc-596e-47f5-b73e-428fe614a59b"}

@array_function_dispatch(_nan_to_num_dispatcher)\\n374: def nan_to_num(x, copy=True, nan=0.0, posinf=None, neginf=None):\\n375:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n376:     Replace NaN with zero and infinity with defined value in\\n383:     `posinf` keyword and -infinity is replaced by the most negative finite\\n384:     floating point values representable by ``x.dtype`` or by the user defined\\n385:     value Whether to create a copy of `x` (True) or to replace values\\n398:         in-place (False). The in-place operation only occurs if\\n399:         casting to an array does not require a copy.\\n400:         Default is True.\\n401:     nan : int, float, optional\\n402:         Value to be used to fill NaN values. If no value is passed\\n403:         then NaN values will be replaced with 0.0.\\n404:     posinf : int, float, optional\\n405:         Value to be used to fill positive infinity values. If no value is\\n410:         passed then negative infinity values will be replaced with a very\\n411:         small (or negative) number.\\n412: \\n413:     Returns\\n414:     -------\\n415:     out : ndarray\\n416:         `x`, with the non-finite values replaced. @array_function_dispatch(_nan_to_num_dispatcher)\\n374: def nan_to_num(x, copy=True, nan=0.0, posinf=None, neginf=None):\\n375:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n376:     Replace NaN with zero and infinity with large finite numbers (default\\n377:     behaviour) or with the numbers defined by the user using the `nan`,\\n378:     `posinf` and/or `neginf` keywords.\\n379: \\n380:     If `x` is inexact, NaN is replaced by zero or by the user defined value in\\n381:     `nan` keyword, infinity is replaced by the largest finite floating point\\n382:     values representable by ``x.dtype`` or by the user defined value in\\n383:     `posinf` keyword and -infinity is replaced by the most negative finite\\n384:     floating point values representable by ``x.dtype`` or by the user defined\\n385:     value in `neginf` keyword.\\n386: \\n387:     For complex dtypes, the above is applied to each of the real and\\n388:     imaginary components of `x` separately.\\n389: \\n390:     If `x` is not inexact, then no replacements are made.\\n391: \\n392:     Parameters\\n393:     ----------\\n394:     x : scalar or array_like\\n395:         Input data.\\n396:     copy : bool, optional\\n397:         Whether to create a copy of `x` (True) or to replace values\\n398:         in-place (False). The in-place operation only occurs if\\n399:         casting to an array does not require a copy.\\n400:         Default is True.\\n401:     nan : int, float, optional\\n402:         Value to be used to fill NaN values. If no value is passed\\n403:         then NaN values will be replaced with 0.0.\\n404:     posinf : int, float, optional\\n405:         Value to be used to fill positive infinity values. If no value is\\n406:         passed then positive infinity values will be replaced with a very\\n407:         large number.\\n408:     neginf : int, float, optional\\n409:         Value to be used to fill negative infinity values. If no value is\\n410:         passed then negative infinity values will be replaced with a very\\n411:         small (or negative) number.\\n412: \\n413:     Returns\\n414:     -------\\n415:     out : ndarray\\n416:         `x`, with the non-finite values replaced. If `copy` is False, this may\\n417:         be `x` itself.\\n418: \\n419:     See Also\\n420:     --------\\n421:     isinf : Shows which elements are positive or negative infinity.\\n422:     isneginf : Shows which elements are negative infinity.\\n423:     isposinf : Shows which elements are positive infinity.\\n424:     isnan : Shows which elements are Not a Number (NaN).\\n425:     isfinite : Shows which elements are finite (not NaN, not infinity)\\n426: \\n427:     Notes\\n428:     -----\\n429:     NumPy uses the IEEE Standard for Binary Floating-Point for Arithmetic\\n430:     (IEEE 754). This means that Not a Number is not equivalent to infinity.\\n431: \\n432:     Examples\\n433:     --------\\n434:     >>> import numpy as np\\n435:     >>> np.nan_to_num(np.inf)\\n436: _real_if_close_dispatcher(a, tol=None):\\n486:     return (a,)\\n487: \\n488: \\n489: @array_function_dispatch(_real_if_close_dispatcher)\\n490: def real_if_close(a, tol=100):\\n491:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n492:     If input is complex with all imaginary parts close to zero, return\\n493:     real parts.\\n494: \\n495:     \\\"Close to zero\\\" is defined as `tol` * (machine epsilon of the type for\\n496:     `a`).\\n497: \\n498:     Parameters\\n499:     ----------\\n500:     a : array_like\\n501:         Input array.\\n502:     tol : float\\n503:         Tolerance in machine epsilons for the complex part of the elements\\n504:         in the array. If the tolerance is <=1, then the absolute tolerance\\n505:         is used.\\n506: \\n507:     Returns\\n508:     -------\\n509:     out : ndarray\\n510:         If `a` is real, the type of `a` is used for the output.  If `a`\\n511:         has complex elements, the returned type is float.\\n512: \\n513:     See Also\\n514:     --------\\n515:     real, imag, angle\\n516: \\n517:     Notes\\n518:     -----\\n519:     Machine epsilon varies from machine to machine and between data types\\n520:     but Python floats on most platforms have a machine epsilon equal to\\n521:     2.2204460492503131e-16.  You can use 'np.finfo(float).eps' to print\\n522:     out the machine epsilon for floats.\\n523: \\n524:     Examples\\n525:     --------\\n526:     >>> import numpy as np\\n527:     >>> @array_function_dispatch(_nan_to_num_dispatcher)\n374: def nan_to_num(x, copy=True, nan=0.0, posinf=None, neginf=None):\n375:     \"\"\"\n376:     Replace NaN with zero and infinity with large finite numbers (default\n377:     behaviour) or with the numbers defined by the user using the `nan`,\n378:     `posinf` and/or `neginf` keywords.\n379: \n380:     If `x` is inexact, NaN is replaced by zero or by the user defined value in\n381:     `nan` keyword, infinity is replaced by the largest finite floating point\n382:     values representable by ``x.dtype`` or by the user defined value in\n383:     `posinf` keyword and -infinity is replaced by the most negative finite\n384:     floating point values representable by ``x.dtype`` or by the user defined\n385:     value in `neginf` keyword.\n386: \n387:     For complex dtypes, the above is applied to each of the real and\n388:     imaginary components of `x` separately.\n389: \n390:     If `x` is not inexact, then no replacements are made.\n391: \n392:     Parameters\n393:     ----------\n394:     x : scalar or array_like\n395:         Input data.\n396:     copy : bool, optional\n397:         Whether to create a copy of `x` (True) or to replace values\n398:         in-place (False). The in-place operation only occurs if\n399:         casting to an array does not require a copy.\n400:         Default is True.\n401:     nan : int, float, optional\n402:         Value to be used to fill NaN values. If no value is passed\n403:         then NaN values will be replaced with 0.0.\n404:     posinf : int, float, optional\n405:         Value to be used to fill positive infinity values. If no value is\n406:         passed then positive infinity values will be replaced with a very\n407:         large number.\n408:     neginf : int, float, optional\n409:         Value to be used to fill negative infinity values. If no value is\n410:         passed then negative infinity values will be replaced with a very\n411:         small (or negative) number.\n412: \n413:     Returns\n414:     -------\n415:     out : ndarray\n416:         `x`, with the non-finite values replaced. If `copy` is False, this may\n417:         be `x` itself.\n418: \n419:     See Also\n420:     --------\n421:     isinf : Shows which elements are positive or negative infinity.\n422:     isneginf : Shows which elements are negative infinity.\n423:     isposinf : Shows which elements are positive infinity.\n424:     isnan : Shows which elements are Not a Number (NaN).\n425:     isfinite : Shows which elements are finite (not NaN, not infinity)\n426: \n427:     Notes\n428:     -----\n429:     NumPy uses the IEEE Standard for Binary Floating-Point for Arithmetic\n430:     (IEEE 754). This means that Not a Number is not equivalent to infinity.\n431: \n432:     Examples\n433:     --------\n434:     >>> import numpy as np\n435:     >>> np.nan_to_num(np.inf)\n436:     1.7976931348623157e+308\n437:     >>> np.nan_to_num(-np.inf)\n438:     -1.7976931348623157e+308\n439:     >>> np.nan_to_num(np.nan)\n440:     0.0\n441:     >>> x = np.array([np.inf, -np.inf, np.nan, np.array([complex(np.inf, np.nan), np.nan, complex(np.nan, np.inf)])\n449:     array([  1.79769313e+308,  -1.79769313e+308,   0.00000000e+000, # may vary\n450:          -1.28000000e+002,
